Jamison Brereton

36 (552)
All Gods
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
9 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Like many All God hymns, this one allots a verse each to a god or group of gods, most named, some not named but obvious from their description, and a few less transparently characterized. The verses whose divinities are clear are 1: Sun; 2: Mitra and Varuс╣Зa; 5: Rudra, 6: Rivers, 7: Maruts (and their mother Pr╠е┼Ыni?); 8: Aramati, P┼лс╣гan, and Bhaga; 9: Maruts and Viс╣гс╣Зu. For verse 3 some schol
ars identify the Wind and Parjanya [Thunder] as the dedicands, but we assign it instead to Soma; verse 4 may belong to both Indra and Aryaman, but we consider aryam├бn here to be used as a descriptor of Indra, rather than as the name of the third member of the ─Аdityan triad, since the other descriptorsтАФ
strong resolution and confounding of the enemyтАЩs battle furyтАФare characteristic of Indra.
The hymn can also be read as a chronological progress through a sacrifice. In verse 1 the fire is kindled at dawn and ritual speech is uttered on the ritual ground. The hymn is mentioned in verse 2, and the preparation of soma in verse 3. The invitation to Indra to come to the sacrifice with his horses is given in verse 4, and the actual sacrifice occurs in verse 5. Although the verse to the rivers (6) does not appear to fit this pattern, it could refer to the waters used to swell the soma stalks

(see also vs. 3) or to other ritual uses of water. The final three verses (7тАУ9) call upon the various gods for wealth and progeny.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods As noted in the published introduction, this hymn can be read as a progress through a sacrifice. Renou (EVP IV.97) follows Hillebrandt in seeing it as a тАЬr├йcitation du pressurage vesp├йral.тАЭ Hillebrandt (Myth. II.128 n. 3) in fact considers it as forming, with VII.37.1-7 and VII.38, an old ┼Ы─Бstra for the Evening (or Third) Pressing.

Although the focus on Indra and the с╣Ъbhus in VII.37 does identify that hymn as associated with the Third Pressing, I do not see that association here. The kindling of the ritual fire that climaxes our vs. 1 (d) suggests rather the Morning Pressing, as does the sunтАЩs sending out the cows in 1b (so also Geldner n. 1b). Moreover, most of the gods named in our hymn are not Third Pressing gods; for example, the Maruts, mentioned twice (vss. 7 and 9) are primarily associated with the Midday Pressing, and though the Third Pressing begins with an ─Аditya cup (which could subsume Mitra and Varuс╣Зa), that pair is prominent in the Morning Pressing and are found here in vs. 2; S┼лrya (vs. 1) is certainly not appropriate to the Evening Pressing. As far as I can, VII.36 and VII.37 are ritually independent.

тАШ рдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдкрддрд┐ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░реНрдЬрдиреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рддрд┐’ (рддреИ. рдЖ. резреж.ремрей) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрдореГрддрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рддрд┐ тАУ тАШрдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд░реНрд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрд░рдиреНрдирдирдВ рддрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдд рдИрджреГрд╢рдВ рдорд╛рд╣рд╛рддреНрдореНрдпрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрддреЗ рдирд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╕реНрдпрдЪрд┐рджрд┐рддреНрдпрдиреЗрди рдкрд╛рджреЗрди рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдкреНрд░рдерд┐рддрд╛ рднреВрдорд┐рдГ рд╕рд╛рдиреБрдирд╛ рд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЫреНрд░рд┐рддреЗрди рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдЙрд░реНрд╡реА рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрд╛ рд╕рддреА рд╡рд┐ рд╕рд╕реНрд░реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╕рд░рддрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкреГрдереБ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд╡рдпрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдирд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдзрд┐ ред рдЕрдзрд┐рдкрд░реА рдЕрдирд░реНрдердХреМ рдЗрддреНрдпрдзреЗрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рд╡рдЪрдиреАрдпрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рд╡рдЪрдиреАрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддреЗ┬░ред рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛ ред рдИрджреГрд╢реЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдПрдзреЗ рдЖрджреАрдкреНрдпрддреЗ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the prayer proceed from the nail of the sacrifice, for S┼лrya with his rays lets loose the waters; thespacious earth spreads (studded) with mountains, and Agni blazes on the extensive plural inс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Y─Бbhir─Бdityastapati ra┼Ыmibhist─Бbhiс╕е parjanyo varс╣гanyo varс╣гati: Taittir─лya ─Аraс╣Зyaka 10.63); Agni blazes:pс╣Ыth─Б prat─лkam adhyedhe agniс╕е: prat─лkam = pс╣Ыthivy─Б avayavam, a portion or member of the earth

Jamison Brereton

Let the sacred formulation go forth from the seat of truth. The Sun with his rays has dispatched the cows outward.
The broad Earth has stretched out on her back. Agni has been kindled on her wide face.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner (n. 1a) and Renou indicate, the opening of this hymn, with pr├б br├бhmaitu (that is, br├бhma etu), is very like the opening of nearby VII.34.1 pr├б ┼Ыukra├нtu (=┼Ыukr─Б╠Бetu) тАж man─лс╣г─Б╠Б, with both referring to the beginning of the ritual day with the dispatch of the poetsтАЩ verbal offering to the gods.

Note the figure v├н тАж sasс╣Ыje (b) / v├н тАж sasre (c), both with 3rd sg. mid. perfects built to phonologically similar roots and compounded (in tmesis) with the same preverb.

Narten (1969 тАЬAi. sс╣Ы in synchronischer und diachronischer SichtтАЭ = Kl. Sch.

135-41) recognizes two synchronically distinct roots тИЪsс╣Ы, primarily act. тАШloslaufen, eilenтАЩ and primarily med. тАШsich ausstreckenтАЩ. The two forms of the med. pf. v├н sasre 51 (here and X.71.4) belong to the latter root; see also K├╝mmel (553). The instr. s─Б╠Бnun─Б I take as idiomatic for тАЬon her back,тАЭ rather than expressing something like тАЬalong the back (of something else).тАЭ The other occurrence of the pf. v├н sasre in X.71.4 contains an explicitly sexual image ut├│ tvasmai tanv├аm v├нsasre, j─Бy├йva p├бtye u┼Ыat─л╠Бsuv─Б╠Бs─Бс╕е тАЬAnd for another she [=Speech] has stretched out her body, like an eager well-dressed wife to her husband,тАЭ and the same picture of feminine yielding is presumably meant here.

Renou curiously takes pс╣Ыth├║ pr├бt─лkam as a тАЬpre-compoundтАЭ modifying Agni, but I follow Geldner in taking it as an acc. construed with ├бdhi, a reference to the part of the earth on which the ritual fire is kindled.

Griffith

LET the prayer issue from the seat of Order, for Surya with his beams hath loosed the cattle.
With lofty ridges earth is far extended, and Agni’s flame hath lit the spacious surface.

Geldner

Die feierliche Rede soll vom Sitze der Wahrheit hinausgehen. Die Sonne hat mit ihren Strahlen die Rinder ausgetrieben. Die Erde hat sich mit dem R├╝cken weit ausgestreckt; das Feuer ist ├╝ber ihre breite Oberfl├дche aufgeflammt.

Grassmann

Vom Sitz des Opfers dringe das Gebet vor, die Sonne trieb durch Strahlen ihre Heerde, Die weite Erde dehnte ihre Fl├дche, und Agni liess sein breites Antlitz strahlen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPowerful Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, to you I offer this new praise as if it were (sacrificial) food; one of you,(Varuс╣Зa). The invincible lord, is the guide to the path (of virtue) Mitra when praised animates men to exertioс╣ЗтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Janam ca mitro yatati bruv─Бс╣Зaс╕е: a repetition of the phrase in RV 3.59.1

Jamison Brereton

This well-twisted (hymn) here do I make anew, like a refreshing drink, for you two, lordly Mitra and Varuс╣Зa.
One of you two, the strong one, is an undeceivable tracer of the track, and (the other), Mitra, arranges the people in their place when
called upon.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My tr. of bruv─Бс╣З├бс╕е тАЬwhen called uponтАЭ follows ThiemeтАЩs (Mitra and Aryaman, p. 69), which in turn follows MeilletтАЩs ([1907] тАЬquand il est invoqu├йтАЭ; see Thieme p. 40). Geldner and Renou both take bruv─Бс╣З├бс╕е as pass./reflex. тАШbe called, call oneselfтАЩ with mitr├бh as predicate (e.g., тАЬder Mitra (Freund) heisstтАЭ). I now think something halfway between is probably correct. When тИЪbr┼л is not cmpded with a preverb, it does not seem to take an acc. of addressee, so my passive version with addressee as subj., тАЬwhen called upon,тАЭ is probably wrong. However, I donтАЩt think itтАЩs a mere naming construction. Rather, ThiemeтАЩs 1st tr. (p. 40) тАЬContract, when named тАжтАЭ conveys the intent better: that, when the word – and god – alliance/Alliance is spoken at the concluding of a pact, the pact acquires its efficacy. JPBтАЩs tr. of the almost identical III.59.1 тАЬMitra arranges the peoples when (Alliance) is declaredтАЭ cleverly plays on the ambiguity of the word mitr├б-, and I would substitute something like that here.

Griffith

O Asuras, O Varuna and Mitra, this hymn to you, like food, anew I offer.
One of you is a strong unerring Leader, and Mitra, speaking, stirreth men to labour.

Geldner

Dieses neueste Loblied bereite ich euch, Mitra und Varuna, ihr Asura┬┤s, wie ein Labsal. Der eine von euch ist ein gewaltiger, untr├╝glicher Sp├╝rer, und der Mitra hei├Яt, eint das Menschenvolk.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe movements of the restless wind sport around; the milk-yielding kine are in good condition; theshowerer genitive rated in the dwelling of the mighty sun has cried aloud in that his plural ce of abiding, (the firmament).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The showerer: acikradad vс╣Ыс╣гabhaс╕е sasmin ┼лdham: parjanya has cried n that firmament, tasmin antarikс╣гeacikradat

Jamison Brereton

The movements of the swooping wind come to rest. The sweet (stalks?) have swelled like milk-cows.
Being born in the seat of great heaven, the bull has roared in the
self-same udder.

Jamison Brereton Notes

y├бjasva тАж dev─Б╠Бn. It is forms (both act. and mid.) compounded with ─Б╠Бthat acquire the meaning тАШobtain by sacrificeтАЩ. I therefore think the abstract qualities fellowship and vitality must be the objects of our sacrifice/worship, standing in for their divine possessor.

I take с╣Ыt├бsya dh─Б╠Бman тАЬdomain of truthтАЭ as referring to the ritual ground (as does S─Бyaс╣Зa.).

GeldnerтАЩs tr. of b─Бbadhe tentatively connects it with тИЪbandh тАШbindтАЩ (flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.), not тИЪb─Бdh тАШ(op)pressтАЩ (see his n. 5c). But тИЪbandh otherwise lacks a pf. in the RV and beginning in the AV its weak forms have a base bedh-. The standard weak 3rd sg. pf.

to тИЪb─Бdh is bab─Бdh├й; see K├╝mmel 330-31. Schaeffer (156) takes b─Бbadhe as an intens.

pres., parallel to badbadh├й with both following the standard perfect in function, and K├╝mmel (331; cf. also 488) seems to follow, though he takes badbadh├й as an intensive perfect, distinguished from the present b─Бbadhe. Since all these stems have a 3rd sg.

ending characteristic of the perfect, I consider at least b─Бbadhe to be a straight perfect, with adjustment of the vowel length of redupl. and root syllable to conform better to such distribution elsewhere in the perfect system; cf. esp. v─Бvс╣Ыdh├й versus vav├бrdha. The intens. badbadh├й then adopted the inflectional patterns of the other two redupl. stems. As for what the verb means here, although v├н тИЪb─Бdh generally has a negative sense тАШthrust away (undesirable things)тАЩ, here I think the same literal sense refers to the godтАЩs pushing out towards us the pс╣Ы╠Бk┼Ыaс╕е тАШfortifying nourishmentsтАЩ we want in exchange for praise. Renou (comm.) suggests a slightly different semantic pathway.

Griffith

The movements of the gliding wind come hither: like cows, the springs are filled to overflowing.
Born in the station e’en of lofty heaven the Bull hath loudly bellowed in this region.

Geldner

Die Anl├дufe des sausenden Windes kommen zur Ruhe; wie Milchk├╝he sind die Lachen angeschwollen. Am Sitz des gro├Яen Himmels geboren hat der Stier im gleichen Euter gebr├╝llt.

Grassmann

Es kommen her des schnellen Windes Z├╝ge, wie K├╝he str├╢mten reichlich s├╝sse Tr├дnke; Der in des hohen Himmels Sitz geborne, er br├╝llte laut der Stier an diesem Euter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHero, Indra, (come to the sacrifice of the man) who, by his adoration, has harnessed (to your car) theseyour favourite, graceful and vigorous horses; may I bring hither Aryaman, the doer of good deeds, who baffles thewrath of the malevolent.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever will yoke with a hymn these two fallow bays of yours, o champion Indra, the two dear ones, good at the chariot, seeking
fodder,
I (as that person) would turn hither the very resolute god of custom [/Aryaman, here = Indra] who confounds the battle fury of the one
who wishes to do harm.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The construction of this vs. is skewed: the first hemistich contains a typical generalizing rel. cl. referring to proper ritual performance (тАЬwho[ever] will yoke тАжтАЭ). It is couched in the 3rd sg. and contains a pres. subjunctive (yun├бjat). In the 2nd hemistich, p─Бda c contains another 3rd sg. rel. cl., this time with a pres. indic. (or possibly subj.) (min─Б╠Бti), but without a ritual focus, and p─Бda d contains a 1st sg.

optative that does relate to the ritual (vavс╣Ыty─Б╠Бm). This ill-assorted trio of clauses has been variously treated. Geldner thinks that both rel. clauses have gods as subject, though not necessarily the same god (see n. 4), and that at least the rel. cl. of c has aryam├бс╣Зam in d as referent of the rel. prn. Renou, mostly flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa., takes a pious human as subject of ab and supplies a main cl. with it. I think rather that d provides the main cl. for ab, with c a distinct rel. cl. dependent on d, and that there is a switch of reference between the 3rd sg. y├бс╕е тАж yun├бjat of the first hemistich and 1st ps. vavс╣Ыty─Бm of d: тАЬIтАЭ am the embodiment of the proper ritual actor as defined in ab. The rel. cl. of c is quite distinct and does indeed depend on ary├бman- in d; the god I wish to bring here to my ritual is the one who can neutralize the battle fury of my (and his) enemy.

Switch of reference between 3rd ps. and 2nd ps., even within a single vs., is extremely common when referring to gods, and I see no reason why a similar switch between 3rd and 1st would not be possible when referring to the poet/ritual officiant. For a 1st ps. version of the 1st p─Бda, cf. I.82.6 yun├бjmi te br├бhmaс╣З─Б ke┼Ы├нn─Б h├бr─л (also III.35.4, VII.19.6).

dh─Бy├║- is a hapax. Grassmann glosses тАШdurstigтАЩ, connecting it to тИЪdh─Б тАШsuckleтАЩ. Oldenberg suggests, quite doubtfully, that it belongs rather to тИЪdh─Бv тАШrunтАЩ, and this suggestion underlies GeldnerтАЩs тАШrennlustigтАЩ; see also AiG II.2.470, where it is explained as showing an exchange between -v- and -y-. EWA s.v. (rightly) rejects this root affiliation, in favor or one suggested by Got┼Н (1st Kl. 179 n. 311) to тИЪdhan1 тАЩid.тАЩ. Renou tr. тАШriches en donsтАЩ, but suggests an association with dh─Б╠Бyas- тАШnourishment, sustenanceтАЩ, bringing us back to GrassmannтАЩs and indeed WhitneyтАЩs (Roots) root etym. to тИЪdh─Б тАШsuckleтАЩ. My тАШseeking fodderтАЩ reflects the same association.

Note the faint phonological figure of (b) sur├бth─Б ┼Ы┼лra dh─Б(yu) / d su(k)r├бt(um).

I follow JPB (─Аdityas, 171-72) in taking ary├бman- here as a descriptor of Indra. As Brereton points out, it makes no sense for Aryaman to appear when the poet is seeking to attract Indra. Moreover, the action of p─Бda c, confounding battle fury, is much more appropriate for Indra (cf., e.g., nearby VII.18.16 ├нndro many├║m manyumy├▓ mim─Бya), who is also the most common referent for the adj. sukr├бtu- тАШvery resoluteтАЩ.

Griffith

May I bring hither with my song, O Indra, wise Aryaman who yokes thy dear Bay Horses,
Voracious, with thy noble car, O Hero, him who defeats the wrath of the malicious.

Geldner

Ihn, der durch seine Lobrede diese deine lieben Falben, die rennlustigen am sch├╢nen Wagen, o Held Indra, anschirren soll, der die b├╢se Absicht des Schadenss├╝chtigen vereitelt, den wohlwollenden Aryaman m├╢chte ich herbringen.

Grassmann

Ihn, der durch Lied an sch├╢nen Wagen schirrte dir, Indra, diese lieben durst’gen Rosse, Und der die Wuth des Schadens├╝cht’gen s├дnftigt, den Arjaman, den holden, lock’ ich zu mir.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the offerers of adoration, engaging (in pious acts), worship (Rudra) in their own hall of sacrifice,(solicitous) of his friendship; praised by the leaders (of rites), he lavishes food (upon them); this most acceptableadoration is addressed to Rudra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The reverent ones worship his fellowship and vitality on the domain of truth itself.
He has thrust outward the fortifying nourishments when being praised by men. This reverence is dearest to Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou in their different ways attempt to wring a more palatable tr.

from yajante than the VP should allow. The problem is that the acc. with this verb here is not a god, the usual object, but two desirable qualities of a god, namely fellowship/companionship and vitality/vigor. In GeldnerтАЩs rendering the reverent ones тАЬrequestтАЭ these qualities (erbitten); in RenouтАЩs they тАЬobtain them by sacrifice.тАЭ But though Renou claims that this is the meaning of medial forms of тИЪyaj, in fact uncompounded middles take the god sacrificed to, just like active forms; cf. nearby 54

Griffith

In their own place of sacrifice adorers worship to gain long life and win his friendship.
He hath poured food on men when they have praised him; be this, the dearest reverence, paid to Rudra.

Geldner

Sie erbitten seine Freundschaft und Lebenskraft demutsvoll, da wo die Wahrheit selbst zur Erscheinung kommt. Von den M├дnnern gepriesen entbindet er die Lebenskr├дfte: dem Rudra sei diese Huldigung die liebste.

Grassmann

Es ehren seine Freundschaft, seine Thatkraft die ehrfurchtsvollen in dem Sitz des Opfers; Ger├╝hmt von M├дnnern liess er Nahrung str├╢men; am liebsten ist ja dies Gebet dem Rudra.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the seventh (stream), Sarasvat─л, the mother of the Sindhu and those rivers that flow copious andfertilizing, bestowing abundance of food, and nourishing (the people) by their waters come at once together.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Themother of the Sindhu: sindhu m─Бt─Б = apam m─Бtс╣Ыbh┼лt─Б, being the mother of the waters

Jamison Brereton

When the glorious ones are bellowing simultaneouslyтАФ(the other rivers and) Sarasvat─л, whose mother is the Sindhu, as seventhтАФ
who are richly fertile, rich in milk, rich in streams, they (come) toward (us), swelling with their own milk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

According to Oldenberg and Geldner, this vs. consists only of dependent clauses, and this is certainly true descriptively: there are two subordinate clauses marked by the subordinating conj. y├бd тАШwhenтАЩ (a) and the rel. prn. y─Б╠Бс╕е (c), one accented verb (suс╣гv├бyanta) in the rel. cl. of c, and no main verbs. In the published translation I take d as a covert main clause, signalled only by the preverb abh├н, with which I supply a verb of motion. However, it is perfectly possible that d is simply a continuation of the rel. cl.

of c, though I do not then know what to do with the abh├н init. in d. Under the interpr.

with cd as rel. clause the 2nd hemistich would simply be тАЬwho are richly fertile, rich in milk, rich in streams, swelling with their own milk.тАЭ In any case, if it lacks a main clause, the vs. cannot be attached either to preceding vs. 5 or following vs. 7; it would have to be an independent if incomplete structure.

The first hemistich lacks a finite verb, and in my view the participle v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е (whether pf. or intens.; K├╝mmel 488 [and Schaeffer by omission] favor the former) serves as predicate. However, both Geldner and Renou supply a verb of motion, presumably on the basis of initial ─Б╠Б: тАЬher(kommen)тАЭ and тАЬar(rivent).тАЭ This is of course possible. Both Geldner and Renou also take the part. v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е as belonging to the pf.

of тИЪva┼Ы тАШdesireтАЩ, whose participle is homonymous with that of тИЪv─Б┼Ы: тАЬzusammenverlangendтАЭ and тАЬriches en d├йsirsтАЭ respectively. Although this cannot be faulted formally, the well-known noise-making quality of rivers (embodied in the very word nad─л╠Б-) provides a more vivid image and, on the other hand, it is not clear what the rivers would be eager for. 55 On the near-hapax suс╣гv├бyanta see my -├бya-Formations (52-53), where I argue that the other occurrence of the stem, act. part. suс╣гv├бyant─л (X.110.6=AV V.27.8) is founded upon this passage and that the form here has been generated in the playful and alliterative context of this vs. (see esp. the following su- adjectives sud├║gh─Бс╕е sudh─Бr─Б╠Бс╕е) loosely to suс╣г┼л╠Б- тАШwell-bearingтАЩ, a connection already suggested by Weber (see Oldenberg). Such a derivation matches the theme of the riversтАЩ burgeoning fertility that dominates the vs. _________ 07
Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda editionтАЩs restoration of the pausal form at the end of c as car├бnti is incorrect; it must be car├бnt─л, as the Pp. has it.

Geldner suggests that the тАШimperishableтАЩ (├бkс╣гar─Б), an esoteric designation for тАШcowтАЩ, is the Dakс╣гiс╣З─Б, while S─Бyaс╣Зa. thinks rather of V─Бc. In this Marut vs. I wonder if it doesnтАЩt refer to their mother Pс╣Ы┼Ыni.

For the phrase y├║jyam тАж ray├нm see VIII.46.19.

The nom. pl. t├й is very oddly positioned, in the middle of both clause and p─Бda, breaking up the NP y├║jyam тАж ray├нm, and not even adjoining the caesura. I have no explanation.

Griffith

Coming together, glorious, loudly roaring - Sarasvati, Mother of Floods, the seventh-
With copious milk, with fair streams, strongly flowing, full swelling with the volume of their water;

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay these joyous and swift-going Maruts protect our sacrifice and our offspring; let not the imperishablegoddess of speech, deserting us, speak (kindly) to our (adversaries); and may both (she and the Marut)associated augment our riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let not the imperishable goddess of speech: m─Б naс╕е parikhyad akс╣гar─Бcaranti = akс╣гar─Б vy─Бpt─Б caranti v─Бgdevat─Б asm─Бn parityaktv─Б asm─Бd vyatirikt─Б m─Б dr─Бkс╣г─лt, let notthe diffusive deity of speech, having abandoned us, look upon our opponents

Jamison Brereton

And these Maruts, exultingтАФlet the prizewinners aid our insight and progeny.
Let not the imperishable (cow? [=Pr╠е┼Ыni?]) overlook us as she roams. They have increased wealth to be harnessed for us.

Griffith

And may the mighty Maruts, too, rejoicing, aid our devotion and protect our offspring.
Let not swift-moving Aksara neglect us: they have increased our own appropriate riches,

Geldner

Auch jene Marut, die sieghaften, sollen begeistert unser Lied und unseren Samen beg├╝nstigen. Nicht m├╢ge uns die weidende Kuh meiden. Diese haben den uns zukommenden Reichtum vermehrt.

Grassmann

Und diese muntern, starken Maruts m├╢gen besch├╝tzen unsre Andacht, unsre Kinder; Nicht fehle uns der Strom, der wandernd rinnet, die Maruts mehrten unsre eigne Habe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInvoke, (worshippers), the unresisting earth, and the adorable hero, P┼лс╣гan; (invoke) Bhaga, theprotector of this our sacrifice, and V─Бja, the sustainer of old, the liberal of gifts to our solemnity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Set in front of yourselves great Devotion [/Aramati], in front P┼лс╣гan, like a hero deserving of the ceremonial distribution;
and Bhaga, who aids this insight of ours, and the prize at its winning, and Plenitude the Gift-Escort.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The NP dhiy├│ avit─Б╠Бram, characterizing Bhaga, reprises the VP dh├нyam тАж avantu in 7b, where the Maruts were the subject.

The phrase s─Бta├║ v─Б╠Бjam in d is somewhat problematic. Geldner takes it, without comment, as equivalent to the common v─Б╠Бjasya s─Бta├║ (e.g., VII.21.7) with a genitive: тАЬbei dem Gewinnen des Preises.тАЭ Renou follows, commenting тАЬseul exemple de s─Бt├нavec r├йgime Acc.тАЭ But this is the problem: although the dative inf. s─Бt├бye regularly takes the acc. (e.g., IX.8.2 s─Бt├бye v├бs┼лni), the loc. to the same stem never does. And in fact even the dative, when construed with v─Б╠Бja-, takes the gen.: v─Б╠Бjasya s─Бt├бye (V.9.7, VI.60.13, IX.7.9, X.93.10). In the one apparent exception, IX.68.7 v─Б╠Бjam ─Б╠Б darс╣гi s─Бt├бye, the acc. is actually object of the main verb. I therefore think that v─Б╠Бjam here has to be an obj. of pr├б тАж kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam, parallel to the divinities and semidivinities in the vs. _________ 09
On niс╣гikta-p─Б╠Б- see Oldenberg and now Scarlatta (306).

I take praj─Б╠Бyai as a quasi-infinitive. See also X.73.5.

Griffith

Bring ye the great Aramati before you, and Pusan as the Hero of the synod,
Bhaga who looks upon this hymn with favour, and, as our strength, the bountiful Purandbi.

тАЬMay this praise come, Maruts, before you; (may it come) before Viс╣гс╣Зu, the guardian of the embryo,with his protecting faculties; may they both bestow upon (me), their adorer, progeny and food; and do you evercherish us with blessings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let this signal-call of ours go to you, o Maruts, to Viс╣гс╣Зu, who protects the poured out (semen) with his help.
And let them establish vitality for the singer to produce progeny. тАУ Do you protect us always with your blessings.

Griffith

May this our song of praise reach you, O Maruts, and Visnu guardian of the future infant.
May they vouchsafe the singer strength for offspring. Preserve us evermore, ye Gods, with blessings.

рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рд╕реНрд╕реЗрд╡рдиреАрдпрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ) (рдЕрдпрдореН) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрдГ) рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдХреНред рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдЩреНрдирд╛рдоред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрез.резрез)ред (рдПрддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреБрдореН) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрдВ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдореН (рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрдкрд╛рдореН) рдпреЛ рдзрд░реНрдореЗ рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрд╛рдирднрд┐рд╖реЗрдХрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдиреН рдкрд╛рддрд┐ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрд┐ рддрдореН (рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ (рдЙрдд) (рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдпреИ) (рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рдп (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН (рдзреБрдГ) рджрдзрддрд┐ (рдпреВрдпрдореН) (рдкрд╛рдд) (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) (рд╕рджрд╛) (рдирдГ) реерепрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╕реБрднрд┐рдГ рд╢реНрд░реЛрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдиреН рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╡рд┐рджреЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдиреБрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреГрд╣реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЛрдиреНрдирддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпреЗрддрд┐ реерепрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рдХреГрддреНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╕реВрдВрдиреА рд╡реЗрджрд╡реЗрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛, рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЬрд╛рдгрдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рд╡ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЗ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░реА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдЪреЗ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрди рдХреЗрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ рд╡ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдЖрдгрд┐ рдЙрдиреНрдирддреА рдХреЗрд▓реА рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее реп рее
